However, they have different approaches and use cases. Let's explore both with an example:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eSuppose you have two branches: \u003ccode\u003efeature\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003emain\u003c/code\u003e, where dir=\"auto\"\u003eHere's how you might use both \u003ccode\u003egit rebase\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003egit merge\u003c/code\u003e in this scenario:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv \u003ccode\u003emain\u003c/code\u003e branch:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"git dir=\"auto\"\u003eMerge the changes from the \u003ccode\u003efeature\u003c/code\u003e branch into \u003ccode\u003emain\u003c/code\u003e:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"snippet-clipboard-content this:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"*   5e0e0e0 (HEAD -\u0026gt; main) Merge branch 'feature'\n|\\\n| * 3a3a3a3 (feature) Add new feature\n|/\n* 1234567 Initial commit\"\u003e\u003cpre class=\"notranslate\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003e*   5e0e0e0 (HEAD -\u0026gt; main) Merge branch 'feature'\n|\\\n| * 3a3a3a3 (feature) Add new feature\n|/\n* 1234567 Initial commit\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe \u003ccode\u003emain\u003c/code\u003e branch now contains the changes from the \u003ccode\u003efeature\u003c/code\u003e branch, and a new merge commit is created to record the merge.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eUsing \u003ccode\u003egit the \u003ccode\u003efeature\u003c/code\u003e branch:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"git dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eRebase the \u003ccode\u003efeature\u003c/code\u003e branch onto \u003ccode\u003emain\u003c/code\u003e:\n\u003cdiv class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"git rebase main\"\u003e\u003cpre class=\"notranslate\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003egit rebase main\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ol\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eIn this case, the commit history would look something like this:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"* New feature commit 3\n* New feature commit 2\n* New feature commit 1\n* Another main branch commit\n* Main branch commit\n* Initial commit\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch1 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eGit Stash and Git Pop: Explained with Examples\u003c/h1\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-git-stash-and-git-pop-explained-with-examples\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Git Stash and Git Pop: Explained with Examples\" href=\"#git-stash-and-git-pop-explained-with-examples\"\u003e\u003csvg data-component=\"Octicon\" class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eGit Stash:\u003c/strong\u003e\nIn Git, the \u003ccode\u003egit stash\u003c/code\u003e command is used to temporarily save changes that you're not ready to commit yet, so you can switch to a different branch or perform other operations without committing incomplete work.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eGit Pop:\u003c/strong\u003e\nThe \u003ccode\u003egit stash pop\u003c/code\u003e command is used to apply the most recent stash and remove it from the stash list. It's like a combination of \u003ccode\u003egit stash apply\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003egit stash drop\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eExample Scenario:\u003c/strong\u003e\nImagine you're working on a feature branch and need to switch to another branch to fix a bug. However, you don't want to commit the incomplete changes on the feature branch. This is where \u003ccode\u003egit stash\u003c/code\u003e comes in handy.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eStep-by-Step Example:\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003col dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eCreate a New Feature Branch:\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"git checkout -b feature/my-feature\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003egit checkout -b feature/my-feature\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eMake Changes:\u003c/strong\u003e\nEdit files in your codebase.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eStash Changes:\u003c/strong\u003e\nStash the changes you've made but aren't ready to commit.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"git stash\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003egit stash\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eSwitch to a Different Branch:\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"git checkout main\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003egit checkout main\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eFix a Bug on Main Branch:\u003c/strong\u003e\nMake necessary changes on the \u003ccode\u003emain\u003c/code\u003e branch to fix a bug.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eCommit Bug Fix:\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"git add \u0026lt;changed_files\u0026gt;\ngit commit -m \u0026quot;Fixed bug\u0026quot;\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003egit add \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003e\u0026lt;\u003c/span\u003echanged_files\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003e\u0026gt;\u003c/span\u003e\ngit commit -m \u003cspan class=\"pl-s\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003eFixed bug\u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eSwitch Back to Feature Branch:\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"git checkout feature/my-feature\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003egit checkout feature/my-feature\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eApply Stashed Changes:\u003c/strong\u003e\nApply the stashed changes from the feature branch.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"git stash pop\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003egit stash pop\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThis will apply the stashed changes and remove the stash from the stash list.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eContinue Working:\u003c/strong\u003e\nNow you can continue working on your feature branch, which now includes the stashed changes.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eCommit Stashed Changes:\u003c/strong\u003e\nIf needed, commit the stashed changes.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"git add \u0026lt;changed_files\u0026gt;\ngit commit -m \u0026quot;Added stashed changes\u0026quot;\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003egit add \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003e\u0026lt;\u003c/span\u003echanged_files\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003e\u0026gt;\u003c/span\u003e\ngit commit -m \u003cspan class=\"pl-s\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003eAdded stashed changes\u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ol\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eAdditional Stash Commands:\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003egit stash list\u003c/code\u003e: Lists all stashes.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003egit stash apply stash@{n}\u003c/code\u003e: Applies a specific stash without removing it from the stash list.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003egit stash drop stash@{n}\u003c/code\u003e: Removes a specific stash from the stash list.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003egit stash clear\u003c/code\u003e: Removes all stashes.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch1 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eGit Revert and Git Reset: Explained with Examples\u003c/h1\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-git-revert-and-git-reset-explained-with-examples\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Git Revert and Git Reset: Explained with Examples\" href=\"#git-revert-and-git-reset-explained-with-examples\"\u003e\u003csvg data-component=\"Octicon\" class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eGit Revert:\u003c/strong\u003e\n\u003ccode\u003egit revert\u003c/code\u003e is used to create a new commit that undoes the changes introduced by a previous commit. It's a safe way to undo changes while preserving the commit history.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eGit Reset:\u003c/strong\u003e\n\u003ccode\u003egit reset\u003c/code\u003e is used to move the current branch pointer to a different commit, effectively resetting the state of the branch. It can be used to discard commits or move branches to a previous state. Be cautious as it can rewrite history.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eExample Scenario:\u003c/strong\u003e\nSuppose you have a repository with the following commit history:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"A --- B --- C --- D (main)\"\u003e\u003cpre class=\"notranslate\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eA --- B --- C --- D (main)\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eCommit A: Initial state\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eCommit B: Added new feature\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eCommit C: Made some changes\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eCommit D: Introduced a bug\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eYou want to undo the changes introduced by commit D and go back to the state after commit C.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eGit Revert:\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003col dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eReverting a Commit:\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"git revert D\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003egit revert D\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThis creates a new commit that undoes the changes from commit D, resulting in:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ol\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"A --- B --- C --- D --- E (main)\"\u003e\u003cpre class=\"notranslate\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eA --- B --- C --- D --- E (main)\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eCommit E: Revert of commit D\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eGit Reset:\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003col dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eSoft Reset:\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"git reset --soft C\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003egit reset --soft C\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThis moves the \u003ccode\u003emain\u003c/code\u003e branch pointer back to commit C, leaving the changes from commit D in the staging area. Your working directory will have the changes from commit D.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"A --- B --- C (main)\n         \\\n          D\"\u003e\u003cpre class=\"notranslate\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eA --- B --- C (main)\n         \\\n          D\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eMixed Reset:\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"git reset --mixed C\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003egit reset --mixed C\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThis is the default mode. It moves the \u003ccode\u003emain\u003c/code\u003e branch pointer to commit C and removes the changes from commit D from the staging area. Your working directory will have the changes from commit D as uncommitted changes.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"A --- B --- C (main)\n         \\\n          D\"\u003e\u003cpre class=\"notranslate\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eA --- B --- C (main)\n         \\\n          D\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eHard Reset:\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"git reset --hard C\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003egit reset --hard C\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThis moves the \u003ccode\u003emain\u003c/code\u003e branch pointer to commit C and discards all changes introduced by commit D. Be cautious with this option as it permanently removes changes.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"A --- B --- C (main)\n         \\\n          D (unreferenced)\"\u003e\u003cpre class=\"notranslate\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eA --- B --- C (main)\n         \\\n          D (unreferenced)\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003egit cherry-pick\u003c/code\u003e is a useful command for selectively applying changes from one commit to another branch. It's particularly handy when you want to bring specific changes from one branch into another without merging the entire branch. Keep in mind that the cherry-picked commit will have a new commit hash, and you should ensure that the changes are still valid in the new context.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ol\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch1 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eBranching Strategy\u003c/h1\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-branching-strategy\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Branching Strategy\" href=\"#branching-strategy\"\u003e\u003csvg data-component=\"Octicon\" class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eEstablishing a robust branching strategy is essential to ensure smooth development, testing, and deployment processes across different environments. Below is a common branching strategy that you can consider for a typical software development lifecycle, including development, testing (QA), pre-production (PPD), production, and disaster recovery (DR) environments.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003col dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eMain/Branch:\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eName: \u003ccode\u003emain\u003c/code\u003e or \u003ccode\u003emaster\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003ePurpose: This is the main branch that holds production-ready code. It's always stable and should ideally reflect the code running in the production environment.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eDevelopment Branch:\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eName: \u003ccode\u003edevelop\u003c/code\u003e or \u003ccode\u003edev\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003ePurpose: All ongoing development work takes place in this branch. New features and bug fixes are merged into this branch. It should be relatively stable but not necessarily production-ready at all times.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eFeature Branches:\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eName: \u003ccode\u003efeature/\u0026lt;feature-name\u0026gt;\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003ePurpose: Each new feature or task gets its own branch, created from the \u003ccode\u003edevelop\u003c/code\u003e branch. Developers work on these branches and merge them back into the \u003ccode\u003edevelop\u003c/code\u003e branch when the feature is complete.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eQA Branch:\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eName: \u003ccode\u003eqa\u003c/code\u003e or \u003ccode\u003etesting\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003ePurpose: Once features are considered complete in the \u003ccode\u003edevelop\u003c/code\u003e branch, they are merged into the \u003ccode\u003eqa\u003c/code\u003e branch for testing. This branch should reflect a stable state for testing purposes.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003ePre-Production Branch:\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eName: \u003ccode\u003eppd\u003c/code\u003e or \u003ccode\u003estaging\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003ePurpose: This branch is used to simulate the production environment closely. After successful QA testing, code is merged from the \u003ccode\u003eqa\u003c/code\u003e branch to the \u003ccode\u003eppd\u003c/code\u003e branch for final validation before deployment.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eProduction Branch:\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eName: \u003ccode\u003eprod\u003c/code\u003e or \u003ccode\u003erelease\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003ePurpose: Once the code is thoroughly tested in the \u003ccode\u003eppd\u003c/code\u003e environment and ready for deployment, it's merged into the \u003ccode\u003eprod\u003c/code\u003e branch and deployed to the production environment.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eDisaster Recovery Branch:\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eName: \u003ccode\u003edr\u003c/code\u003e or \u003ccode\u003ebackup\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003ePurpose: This branch holds code that is identical to the currently deployed production code. It's useful for disaster recovery scenarios, allowing rapid deployment of the latest stable code in case of critical issues.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ol\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch1 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e50 Git commands\u003c/h1\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-50-git-commands\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: 50 Git commands\" href=\"#50-git-commands\"\u003e\u003csvg data-component=\"Octicon\" class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e1. \u003ccode\u003egit init\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e\nInitializes a new Git repository.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"$ git init\nInitialized empty Git repository in /path/to/repository/\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e$ git init\nInitialized empty Git repository \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003ein\u003c/span\u003e /path/to/repository/\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e2. \u003ccode\u003egit clone\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e\nClones a remote repository to your local machine.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"$ git clone https://github.com/username/repository.git\nCloning into 'repository'...\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e$ git clone https://github.com/username/repository.git\nCloning into \u003cspan class=\"pl-s\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e'\u003c/span\u003erepository\u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e'\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/span\u003e...\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e3. \u003ccode\u003egit add\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e\nStages changes for commit.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"$ git add file.txt\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e$ git add file.txt\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e4. \u003ccode\u003egit status\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e\nShows the status of the working directory and staged changes.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"$ git status\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e$ git status\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e5. \u003ccode\u003egit commit\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e\nCommits staged changes.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"$ git commit -m \u0026quot;Added new feature\u0026quot;\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e$ git commit -m \u003cspan class=\"pl-s\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003eAdded new feature\u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e6. \u003ccode\u003egit log\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e\nDisplays commit history.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"$ git log\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e$ git log\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e7. \u003ccode\u003egit diff\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e\nShows differences between working directory and staged changes.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"$ git diff\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e$ git diff\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e8. \u003ccode\u003egit branch\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e\nLists branches.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"$ git branch\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e$ git branch\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e9. \u003ccode\u003egit checkout\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e\nSwitches branches or restores files.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight branch_name\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e10. \u003ccode\u003egit merge\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e\nMerges changes from one branch into another.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"$ git merge feature_branch\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e$ git merge feature_branch\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e11. \u003ccode\u003egit pull\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e\nFetches and integrates changes from a remote repository.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"$ git pull origin master\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e$ git pull origin master\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e12. \u003ccode\u003egit push\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e\nPushes changes to a remote repository.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight master\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e13. \u003ccode\u003egit remote\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e\nManages remote dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e14. \u003ccode\u003egit fetch\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e\nDownloads objects and refs from a remote repository.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight origin\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e15. \u003ccode\u003egit stash\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e\nTemporarily stores changes to work on something else.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"$ git manages tags for specific commits.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"$ git tag v1.0.0\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e$ git tag v1.0.0\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e17. \u003ccode\u003egit reset\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e\nUnstages changes or moves the HEAD to a specific commit.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"$ git reset HEAD file.txt\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e$ git reset HEAD file.txt\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e18. \u003ccode\u003egit rebase\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e\nReapplies commits on top of another base.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"$ git rebase master\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e$ git rebase master\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e19. \u003ccode\u003egit config\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e\nSets configuration options.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"$ git config --global user.name \u0026quot;Your Name\u0026quot;\n$ git config --global user.email \u0026quot;your.email@example.com\u0026quot;\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e$ git config --global user.name \u003cspan class=\"pl-s\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003eYour Name\u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\n$ git config --global user.email \u003cspan class=\"pl-s\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003eyour.email@example.com\u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e20. \u003ccode\u003egit log --oneline\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e\nDisplays compact commit history.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"$ git log --oneline\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e$ git log --oneline\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e21. \u003ccode\u003egit show\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e\nShows information about a commit.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"$ git show commit_hash\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e$ git show commit_hash\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e22. \u003ccode\u003egit cherry-pick\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e\nApplies a commit from one branch to another.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"$ git cherry-pick commit_hash\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e$ git cherry-pick Git Commands:**","","1. **git init:** Initialize a new Git repository.","   ","   ```bash","   git init","   ```","","2. **git clone:** Create a copy of a remote repository on your local machine.","   ","   ```bash","   git clone \u003crepository_url\u003e","   ```","","3. **git add:** Stage changes for commit.","   ","   ```bash","   git add \u003cfilename\u003e","   ```","","4. **git commit:** Create a new commit with staged changes.","   ","   ```bash","   git commit -m \"Commit message\"","   ```","","5. **git push:** Upload local commits to a remote repository.","   ","   ```bash","   git push origin \u003cbranch_name\u003e","   ```","","6. **git pull:** Fetch remote changes and integrate them into the current branch.","   ","   ```bash","   git pull origin \u003cbranch_name\u003e","   ```","","7. **git branch:** List, create, or delete branches.","   ","   ```bash","   git branch","   git branch \u003cbranch_name\u003e","   git branch -d \u003cbranch_name\u003e","   ```","","8. **git checkout:** Switch to a different branch or commit.","   ","   ```bash","   git checkout \u003cbranch_name\u003e","   ```","","9. **git merge:** Combine changes from one branch into another.","   ","   ```bash","   git merge \u003csource_branch\u003e","   ```","","10. **git pull request:** Create a pull request on platforms like GitHub or GitLab.","","### Workflow Example:","1. **Create a New Feature Branch:**","   ","   ```bash","   git checkout -b feature/my-feature","   ```","","2. **Make Changes:**","   Edit files in your codebase.","","3. **Stage and Commit Changes:**","   ","   ```bash","   git add \u003cchanged_files\u003e","   git commit -m \"Added new feature\"","   ```","","4. **Push Changes to Remote:**","   ","   ```bash","   git push origin feature/my-feature","   ```","","5. **Create a Pull Request:**","   On your remote repository's platform (e.g., GitHub), create a pull request from your feature branch to the main branch. Discuss, review, and test changes if necessary.","","6. **Merge the Pull Request:**","   After approval, merge the pull request on the remote platform.","","7. **Update Local Main Branch:**","   ","   ```bash","   git checkout main","   git pull origin main","   ```","","8. **Delete the Feature Branch (Optional):**","   ","   ```bash","   git branch -d feature/my-feature","   ```","","This covers the basics of Git and GitHub. For more advanced topics, refer to the official Git documentation and GitHub's documentation.`","","# Git Merge \u0026 Git Rebase","","Both `git rebase` and `git merge` are used to integrate changes from one branch into another. However, they have different approaches and use cases. Let's explore both with an example:","","Suppose you have two branches: `feature` and `main`, where `main` is your main development branch, and `feature` contains a new feature you've been working on.","","Here's how you might use both `git rebase` and `git merge` in this scenario:","","### Using `git merge`:","","1. Switch to the `main` branch:","   ```","   git checkout main","   ```","","2. Merge the changes from the `feature` branch into `main`:","   ```","   git merge feature","   ```","","In this case, the commit history would look something like this:","","```","*   5e0e0e0 (HEAD -\u003e main) Merge branch 'feature'","|\\","| * 3a3a3a3 (feature) Add new feature","|/","* 1234567 Initial commit","```","","The `main` branch now contains the changes from the `feature` branch, and a new merge commit is created to record the merge.","","### Using `git rebase`:",""," Switch to the `feature` branch:","   ```","   git checkout feature","   ```","","2. Rebase the `feature` branch onto `main`:","   ```","   git rebase main","   ```","","In this case, the commit history would look something like this:","","```","* New feature commit 3","* New feature commit 2","* New feature commit 1","* Another main branch commit","* Main branch commit","* Initial commit","```","","# Git Stash and Git Pop: Explained with Examples","","**Git Stash:**","In Git, the `git stash` command is used to temporarily save changes that you're not ready to commit yet, so you can switch to a different branch or perform other operations without committing incomplete work.","","**Git Pop:**","The `git stash pop` command is used to apply the most recent stash and remove it from the stash list. It's like a combination of `git stash apply` and `git stash drop`.","","**Example Scenario:**","Imagine you're working on a feature branch and need to switch to another branch to fix a bug. However, you don't want to commit the incomplete changes on the feature branch. This is where `git stash` comes in handy.","","**Step-by-Step Example:**","","1. **Create a New Feature Branch:**","   ","   ```bash","   git checkout -b feature/my-feature","   ```","","2. **Make Changes:**","   Edit files in your codebase.","","3. **Stash Changes:**","   Stash the changes you've made but aren't ready to commit.","   ","   ```bash","   git stash","   ```","","4. **Switch to a Different Branch:**","   ","   ```bash","   git checkout main","   ```","","5. **Fix a Bug on Main Branch:**","   Make necessary changes on the `main` branch to fix a bug.","","6. **Commit Bug Fix:**","   ","   ```bash","   git add \u003cchanged_files\u003e","   git commit -m \"Fixed bug\"","   ```","","7. **Switch Back to Feature Branch:**","   ","   ```bash","   git checkout feature/my-feature","   ```","","8. **Apply Stashed Changes:**","   Apply the stashed changes from the feature branch.","   ","   ```bash","   git stash pop","   ```","","   This will apply the stashed changes and remove the stash from the stash list.","","9. **Continue Working:**","   Now you can continue working on your feature branch, which now includes the stashed changes.","","10. **Commit Stashed Changes:**","    If needed, commit the stashed changes.","   ","    ```bash","    git add \u003cchanged_files\u003e","    git commit -m \"Added stashed changes\"","    ```","    ","**Additional Stash Commands:**","","- `git stash list`: Lists all stashes.","- `git stash apply stash@{n}`: Applies a specific stash without removing it from the stash list.","- `git stash drop stash@{n}`: Removes a specific stash from the stash list.","- `git stash clear`: Removes all stashes.","# Git Revert and Git Reset: Explained with Examples","","**Git Revert:**","`git revert` is used to create a new commit that undoes the changes introduced by a previous commit. It's a safe way to undo changes while preserving the commit history.","","**Git Reset:**","`git reset` is used to move the current branch pointer to a different commit, effectively resetting the state of the branch. It can be used to discard commits or move branches to a previous state. Be cautious as it can rewrite history.","","**Example Scenario:**","Suppose you have a repository with the following commit history:","","```","A --- B --- C --- D (main)","```","","- Commit A: Initial state","- Commit B: Added new feature","- Commit C: Made some changes","- Commit D: Introduced a bug","","You want to undo the changes introduced by commit D and go back to the state after commit C.","","**Git Revert:**","1. **Reverting a Commit:**","   ","   ```bash","   git revert D","   ```","","   This creates a new commit that undoes the changes from commit D, resulting in:","","```","A --- B --- C --- D --- E (main)","```","","- Commit E: Revert of commit D","","**Git Reset:**","1. **Soft Reset:**","   ","   ```bash","   git reset --soft C","   ```","","   This moves the `main` branch pointer back to commit C, leaving the changes from commit D in the staging area. Your working directory will have the changes from commit D.","","   ```","   A --- B --- C (main)","            \\","             D","   ```","","2. **Mixed Reset:**","   ","   ```bash","   git reset --mixed C","   ```","","   This is the default mode. It moves the `main` branch pointer to commit C and removes the changes from commit D from the staging area. Your working directory will have the changes from commit D as uncommitted changes.","","   ```","   A --- B --- C (main)","            \\","             D","   ```","","3. **Hard Reset:**","   ","   ```bash","   git reset --hard C","   ```","","   This moves the `main` branch pointer to commit C and discards all changes introduced by commit D. Be cautious with this option as it permanently removes changes.","","   ```","   A --- B --- C (main)","            \\","             D (unreferenced)","   ```","   `git cherry-pick` is a useful command for selectively applying changes from one commit to another branch. It's particularly handy when you want to bring specific changes from one branch into another without merging the entire branch. Keep in mind that the cherry-picked commit will have a new commit hash, and you should ensure that the changes are still valid in the new context.","","# Branching Strategy","Establishing a robust branching strategy is essential to ensure smooth development, testing, and deployment processes across different environments. Below is a common branching strategy that you can consider for a typical software development lifecycle, including development, testing (QA), pre-production (PPD), production, and disaster recovery (DR) environments.","","","1. **Main/Branch:**","   - Name: `main` or `master`","   - Purpose: This is the main branch that holds production-ready code. It's always stable and should ideally reflect the code running in the production environment.","","2. **Development Branch:**","   - Name: `develop` or `dev`","   - Purpose: All ongoing development work takes place in this branch. New features and bug fixes are merged into this branch. It should be relatively stable but not necessarily production-ready at all times.","","3. **Feature Branches:**","   - Name: `feature/\u003cfeature-name\u003e`","   - Purpose: Each new feature or task gets its own branch, created from the `develop` branch. Developers work on these branches and merge them back into the `develop` branch when the feature is complete.","","4. **QA Branch:**","   - Name: `qa` or `testing`","   - Purpose: Once features are considered complete in the `develop` branch, they are merged into the `qa` branch for testing. This branch should reflect a stable state for testing purposes.","","5. **Pre-Production Branch:**","   - Name: `ppd` or `staging`","   - Purpose: This branch is used to simulate the production environment closely. After successful QA testing, code is merged from the `qa` branch to the `ppd` branch for final validation before deployment.","","6. **Production Branch:**","   - Name: `prod` or `release`","   - Purpose: Once the code is thoroughly tested in the `ppd` environment and ready for deployment, it's merged into the `prod` branch and deployed to the production environment.","","7. **Disaster Recovery Branch:**","   - Name: `dr` or `backup`","   - Purpose: This branch holds code that is identical to the currently deployed production code. It's useful for disaster recovery scenarios, allowing rapid deployment of the latest stable code in case of critical issues.","# 50 Git commands","","**1. `git init`**","Initializes a new Git repository.","","```bash","$ git init","Initialized empty Git repository in /path/to/repository/","```","","**2. `git clone`**","Clones a remote repository to your local machine.","","```bash","$ git clone https://github.com/username/repository.git","Cloning into 'repository'...","```","","**3. `git add`**","Stages changes for commit.","","```bash","$ git add file.txt","```","","**4. `git status`**","Shows the status of the working directory and staged changes.","","```bash","$ git status","```","","**5. `git commit`**","Commits staged changes.","","```bash","$ git commit -m \"Added new feature\"","```","","**6. `git log`**","Displays commit history.","","```bash","$ git log","```","","**7. `git diff`**","Shows differences between working directory and staged changes.","","```bash","$ git diff","```","","**8. `git branch`**","Lists branches.","","```bash","$ git branch","```","","**9. `git checkout`**","Switches branches or restores files.","","```bash","$ git checkout branch_name","```","","**10. `git merge`**","Merges changes from one branch into another.","","```bash","$ git merge feature_branch","```","","**11. `git pull`**","Fetches and integrates changes from a remote repository.","","```bash","$ git pull origin master","```","","**12. `git push`**","Pushes changes to a remote repository.","","```bash","$ git push origin master","```","","**13. `git remote`**","Manages remote repositories.","","```bash","$ git remote add origin https://github.com/username/repository.git","```","","**14. `git fetch`**","Downloads objects and refs from a remote repository.","","```bash","$ git fetch origin","```","","**15. `git stash`**","Temporarily stores changes to work on something else.","","```bash","$ git stash","```","","**16. `git tag`**","Creates and manages tags for specific commits.","","```bash","$ git tag v1.0.0","```","","**17. `git reset`**","Unstages changes or moves the HEAD to a specific commit.","","```bash","$ git reset HEAD file.txt","```","","**18. `git rebase`**","Reapplies commits on top of another base.","","```bash","$ git rebase master","```","","**19. `git config`**","Sets configuration options.","","```bash","$ git config --global user.name \"Your Name\"","$ git config --global user.email \"your.email@example.com\"","```","","**20. `git log --oneline`**","Displays compact commit history.","","```bash","$ git log --oneline","```","","**21. `git show`**","Shows information about a commit.","","```bash","$ git show commit_hash","```","","**22. `git cherry-pick`**","Applies a commit from one branch to another.","","```bash","$ git cherry-pick commit_hash","```","","**23. `git rm`**","Removes files from the working directory and stages the removal.","","```bash","$ git rm file.txt","```","","**24. `git revert`**","Creates a new commit that undoes changes from a previous commit.","","```bash","$ git revert commit_hash","```","","**25. `git reflog`**","Displays the history of HEAD positions.","","```bash","$ git reflog","```","","**26. `git clean`**","Removes untracked files and directories from the working directory.","","```bash","$ git clean -n  # Dry-run","$ git clean -f  # Force removal","```","","**27. `git tag -a`**","Creates an annotated tag with a message.","","```bash","$ git tag -a v1.0.0 -m \"Version 1.0.0\"","```","","**28. `git log --graph`**","Displays commit history as a graph.","","```bash","$ git log --graph --oneline","```","","**29. `git config --list`**","Lists all Git configuration settings.","","```bash","$ git config --list","```","","**30. `git log --since` / `git log --until`**","Displays commit history within a time range.","","```bash","$ git log --since=\"2 weeks ago\"","$ git log --until=\"2023-07-01\"","```","","**31. `git cherry`**","Shows commits that have not been merged.","","```bash","$ git cherry master feature_branch","```","","**32. `git revert --no-commit`**","Reverts changes interactively without committing.","","```bash","$ git revert --no-commit commit_range","```","","**33. `git log --author`**","Filters commit history by author.","","```bash","$ git log --author=\"John Doe\"","```","","**34. `git log --stat`**","Displays file statistics with commit history.","","```bash","$ git log --stat","```","","**35. `git blame`**","Shows who last modified each line in a file.","","```bash","$ git blame file.txt","```","","**36. `git tag -d`**","Deletes a tag.","","```bash","$ git tag -d v1.0.0","```","","**37. `git log -p`**","Displays commit history with patch diffs.","","```bash","$ git log -p","```","","**38. `git rev-parse`**","Converts a revision string into a SHA-1 hash.","","```bash","$ git rev-parse HEAD","```","","**39. `git remote -v`**","Lists remote repositories and their URLs.","","```bash","$ git remote -v","```","","**40. `git log --decorate`**","Displays references (branches, tags) in commit history.","","```bash","$ git log --decorate","```","","**41. `git bisect`**","Performs a binary search to find a faulty commit.","","```bash","$ git bisect start","$ git bisect good \u003ccommit\u003e","$ git bisect bad \u003ccommit\u003e","$ git bisect reset","```","","**42. `git log --grep`**","Searches commit messages for a specific keyword.","","```bash","$ git log --grep=\"bug fix\"","```","","**43. `git log --name-only`**","Displays only file names in commit history.","","```bash","$ git log --name-only","```","","**44. `git rebase -i`**","Interactively rewrites commit history.","","```bash","$ git rebase -i HEAD~3","```","","**45. `git log --before` / `git log --after`**","Displays commit history before/after a specific date.","","```bash","$ git log --before=\"2023-01-01\"","$ git log --after=\"2022-01-01\"","```","","**46. `git checkout -b`**","Creates a new branch and switches to it.","","```bash","$ git checkout -b new_feature","```","","**47. `git log --cherry-pick`**","Shows commits that have been cherry-picked.","","```bash","$ git log --cherry-pick master..feature_branch","```","","**48. `git log -S`**","Searches for changes that added or removed a specific string.","","```bash","$ git log -S \"function_name\"","```","","**49. `git reflog expire`**","Expires old reflog entries.","","```bash","$ git reflog expire --expire=30.days refs/heads/master","```","","**50. `git commit --amend`**","Modifies the most recent commit.","","```bash","$ git commit
