actions</span></div></div></div></div><div></div></div><div class="BlobViewContent-module__blobContentWrapper__JS0W6"><section aria-labelledby="file-name-id-wide file-name-id-mobile" class="BlobContent-module__blobContentSection__VOgZq BlobContent-module__blobContentSectionMarkdown__mPLOK" style="margin-top:46px"><div class="js-snippet-clipboard-copy-unpositioned BlobContent-module__markdownBlob__T8jpG" data-hpc="true" containertiming="hpc"><article class="markdown-body entry-content container-lg" itemprop="text"><p dir="auto"><strong>Basic Git Commands:</strong></p>
<ol dir="auto">
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>git init:</strong> Initialize a new Git repository.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="git init"><pre>git init</pre></div>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>git clone:</strong> Create a copy of a remote repository on your local machine.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="git clone &lt;repository_url&gt;"><pre>git clone <span class="pl-k">&lt;</span>repository_url<span class="pl-k">&gt;</span></pre></div>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>git add:</strong> Stage changes for commit.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="git add &lt;filename&gt;"><pre>git add <span class="pl-k">&lt;</span>filename<span class="pl-k">&gt;</span></pre></div>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>git commit:</strong> Create a new commit with staged changes.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="git commit -m &quot;Commit message&quot;"><pre>git commit -m <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>Commit message<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span></pre></div>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>git push:</strong> Upload local commits to a remote repository.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="git push origin &lt;branch_name&gt;"><pre>git push origin <span class="pl-k">&lt;</span>branch_name<span class="pl-k">&gt;</span></pre></div>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>git pull:</strong> Fetch remote changes and integrate them into the current branch.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="git pull origin &lt;branch_name&gt;"><pre>git pull origin <span class="pl-k">&lt;</span>branch_name<span class="pl-k">&gt;</span></pre></div>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>git branch:</strong> List, create, or delete branches.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="git branch
git branch &lt;branch_name&gt;
git branch -d &lt;branch_name&gt;"><pre>git branch
git branch <span class="pl-k">&lt;</span>branch_name<span class="pl-k">&gt;</span>
git branch -d <span class="pl-k">&lt;</span>branch_name<span class="pl-k">&gt;</span></pre></div>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>git checkout:</strong> Switch to a different branch or commit.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="git checkout &lt;branch_name&gt;"><pre>git checkout <span class="pl-k">&lt;</span>branch_name<span class="pl-k">&gt;</span></pre></div>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>git merge:</strong> Combine changes from one branch into another.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="git merge &lt;source_branch&gt;"><pre>git merge <span class="pl-k">&lt;</span>source_branch<span class="pl-k">&gt;</span></pre></div>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>git pull request:</strong> Create a pull request on platforms like GitHub or GitLab.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Workflow Example:</h3><a id="user-content-workflow-example" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Workflow Example:" href="#workflow-example"><svg data-component="Octicon" class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<ol dir="auto">
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Create a New Feature Branch:</strong></p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="git checkout -b feature/my-feature"><pre>git checkout -b feature/my-feature</pre></div>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Make Changes:</strong>
Edit files in your codebase.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Stage and Commit Changes:</strong></p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="git add &lt;changed_files&gt;
git commit -m &quot;Added new feature&quot;"><pre>git add <span class="pl-k">&lt;</span>changed_files<span class="pl-k">&gt;</span>
git commit -m <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>Added new feature<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span></pre></div>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Push Changes to Remote:</strong></p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="git push origin feature/my-feature"><pre>git push origin feature/my-feature</pre></div>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Create a Pull Request:</strong>
On your remote repository's platform (e.g., GitHub), create a pull request from your feature branch to the main branch. Discuss, review, and test changes if necessary.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Merge the Pull Request:</strong>
After approval, merge the pull request on the remote platform.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Update Local Main Branch:</strong></p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="git checkout main
git pull origin main"><pre>git checkout main
git pull origin main</pre></div>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Delete the Feature Branch (Optional):</strong></p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="git branch -d feature/my-feature"><pre>git branch -d feature/my-feature</pre></div>
</li>
</ol>
<p dir="auto">This covers the basics of Git and GitHub. For more advanced topics, refer to the official Git documentation and GitHub's documentation.`</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h1 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Git Merge &amp; Git Rebase</h1><a id="user-content-git-merge--git-rebase" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Git Merge &amp; Git Rebase" href="#git-merge--git-rebase"><svg data-component="Octicon" class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Both <code>git rebase</code> and <code>git merge</code> are used to integrate changes from one branch into another. However, they have different approaches and use cases. Let's explore both with an example:</p>
<p dir="auto">Suppose you have two branches: <code>feature</code> and <code>main</code>, where <code>main</code> is your main development branch, and <code>feature</code> contains a new feature you've been working on.</p>
<p dir="auto">Here's how you might use both <code>git rebase</code> and <code>git merge</code> in this scenario:</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Using <code>git merge</code>:</h3><a id="user-content-using-git-merge" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Using git merge:" href="#using-git-merge"><svg data-component="Octicon" class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<ol dir="auto">
<li>
<p dir="auto">Switch to the <code>main</code> branch:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="git checkout main"><pre class="notranslate"><code>git checkout main
</code></pre></div>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto">Merge the changes from the <code>feature</code> branch into <code>main</code>:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="git merge feature"><pre class="notranslate"><code>git merge feature
</code></pre></div>
</li>
</ol>
<p dir="auto">In this case, the commit history would look something like this:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="*   5e0e0e0 (HEAD -&gt; main) Merge branch 'feature'
|\
| * 3a3a3a3 (feature) Add new feature
|/
* 1234567 Initial commit"><pre class="notranslate"><code>*   5e0e0e0 (HEAD -&gt; main) Merge branch 'feature'
|\
| * 3a3a3a3 (feature) Add new feature
|/
* 1234567 Initial commit
</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">The <code>main</code> branch now contains the changes from the <code>feature</code> branch, and a new merge commit is created to record the merge.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Using <code>git rebase</code>:</h3><a id="user-content-using-git-rebase" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Using git rebase:" href="#using-git-rebase"><svg data-component="Octicon" class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Switch to the <code>feature</code> branch:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="git checkout feature"><pre class="notranslate"><code>git checkout feature
</code></pre></div>
<ol start="2" dir="auto">
<li>Rebase the <code>feature</code> branch onto <code>main</code>:
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="git rebase main"><pre class="notranslate"><code>git rebase main
</code></pre></div>
</li>
</ol>
<p dir="auto">In this case, the commit history would look something like this:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="* New feature commit 3
* New feature commit 2
* New feature commit 1
* Another main branch commit
* Main branch commit
* Initial commit"><pre class="notranslate"><code>* New feature commit 3
* New feature commit 2
* New feature commit 1
* Another main branch commit
* Main branch commit
* Initial commit
</code></pre></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h1 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Git Stash and Git Pop: Explained with Examples</h1><a id="user-content-git-stash-and-git-pop-explained-with-examples" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Git Stash and Git Pop: Explained with Examples" href="#git-stash-and-git-pop-explained-with-examples"><svg data-component="Octicon" class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Git Stash:</strong>
In Git, the <code>git stash</code> command is used to temporarily save changes that you're not ready to commit yet, so you can switch to a different branch or perform other operations without committing incomplete work.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Git Pop:</strong>
The <code>git stash pop</code> command is used to apply the most recent stash and remove it from the stash list. It's like a combination of <code>git stash apply</code> and <code>git stash drop</code>.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Example Scenario:</strong>
Imagine you're working on a feature branch and need to switch to another branch to fix a bug. However, you don't want to commit the incomplete changes on the feature branch. This is where <code>git stash</code> comes in handy.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Step-by-Step Example:</strong></p>
<ol dir="auto">
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Create a New Feature Branch:</strong></p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="git checkout -b feature/my-feature"><pre>git checkout -b feature/my-feature</pre></div>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Make Changes:</strong>
Edit files in your codebase.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Stash Changes:</strong>
Stash the changes you've made but aren't ready to commit.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="git stash"><pre>git stash</pre></div>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Switch to a Different Branch:</strong></p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="git checkout main"><pre>git checkout main</pre></div>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Fix a Bug on Main Branch:</strong>
Make necessary changes on the <code>main</code> branch to fix a bug.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Commit Bug Fix:</strong></p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="git add &lt;changed_files&gt;
git commit -m &quot;Fixed bug&quot;"><pre>git add <span class="pl-k">&lt;</span>changed_files<span class="pl-k">&gt;</span>
git commit -m <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>Fixed bug<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span></pre></div>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Switch Back to Feature Branch:</strong></p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="git checkout feature/my-feature"><pre>git checkout feature/my-feature</pre></div>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Apply Stashed Changes:</strong>
Apply the stashed changes from the feature branch.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="git stash pop"><pre>git stash pop</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">This will apply the stashed changes and remove the stash from the stash list.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Continue Working:</strong>
Now you can continue working on your feature branch, which now includes the stashed changes.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Commit Stashed Changes:</strong>
If needed, commit the stashed changes.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="git add &lt;changed_files&gt;
git commit -m &quot;Added stashed changes&quot;"><pre>git add <span class="pl-k">&lt;</span>changed_files<span class="pl-k">&gt;</span>
git commit -m <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>Added stashed changes<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span></pre></div>
</li>
</ol>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Additional Stash Commands:</strong></p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><code>git stash list</code>: Lists all stashes.</li>
<li><code>git stash apply stash@{n}</code>: Applies a specific stash without removing it from the stash list.</li>
<li><code>git stash drop stash@{n}</code>: Removes a specific stash from the stash list.</li>
<li><code>git stash clear</code>: Removes all stashes.</li>
</ul>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h1 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Git Revert and Git Reset: Explained with Examples</h1><a id="user-content-git-revert-and-git-reset-explained-with-examples" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Git Revert and Git Reset: Explained with Examples" href="#git-revert-and-git-reset-explained-with-examples"><svg data-component="Octicon" class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Git Revert:</strong>
<code>git revert</code> is used to create a new commit that undoes the changes introduced by a previous commit. It's a safe way to undo changes while preserving the commit history.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Git Reset:</strong>
<code>git reset</code> is used to move the current branch pointer to a different commit, effectively resetting the state of the branch. It can be used to discard commits or move branches to a previous state. Be cautious as it can rewrite history.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Example Scenario:</strong>
Suppose you have a repository with the following commit history:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="A --- B --- C --- D (main)"><pre class="notranslate"><code>A --- B --- C --- D (main)
</code></pre></div>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Commit A: Initial state</li>
<li>Commit B: Added new feature</li>
<li>Commit C: Made some changes</li>
<li>Commit D: Introduced a bug</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto">You want to undo the changes introduced by commit D and go back to the state after commit C.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Git Revert:</strong></p>
<ol dir="auto">
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Reverting a Commit:</strong></p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="git revert D"><pre>git revert D</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">This creates a new commit that undoes the changes from commit D, resulting in:</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="A --- B --- C --- D --- E (main)"><pre class="notranslate"><code>A --- B --- C --- D --- E (main)
</code></pre></div>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Commit E: Revert of commit D</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Git Reset:</strong></p>
<ol dir="auto">
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Soft Reset:</strong></p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="git reset --soft C"><pre>git reset --soft C</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">This moves the <code>main</code> branch pointer back to commit C, leaving the changes from commit D in the staging area. Your working directory will have the changes from commit D.</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="A --- B --- C (main)
         \
          D"><pre class="notranslate"><code>A --- B --- C (main)
         \
          D
</code></pre></div>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Mixed Reset:</strong></p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="git reset --mixed C"><pre>git reset --mixed C</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">This is the default mode. It moves the <code>main</code> branch pointer to commit C and removes the changes from commit D from the staging area. Your working directory will have the changes from commit D as uncommitted changes.</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="A --- B --- C (main)
         \
          D"><pre class="notranslate"><code>A --- B --- C (main)
         \
          D
</code></pre></div>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Hard Reset:</strong></p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="git reset --hard C"><pre>git reset --hard C</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">This moves the <code>main</code> branch pointer to commit C and discards all changes introduced by commit D. Be cautious with this option as it permanently removes changes.</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="A --- B --- C (main)
         \
          D (unreferenced)"><pre class="notranslate"><code>A --- B --- C (main)
         \
          D (unreferenced)
</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><code>git cherry-pick</code> is a useful command for selectively applying changes from one commit to another branch. It's particularly handy when you want to bring specific changes from one branch into another without merging the entire branch. Keep in mind that the cherry-picked commit will have a new commit hash, and you should ensure that the changes are still valid in the new context.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h1 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Branching Strategy</h1><a id="user-content-branching-strategy" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Branching Strategy" href="#branching-strategy"><svg data-component="Octicon" class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Establishing a robust branching strategy is essential to ensure smooth development, testing, and deployment processes across different environments. Below is a common branching strategy that you can consider for a typical software development lifecycle, including development, testing (QA), pre-production (PPD), production, and disaster recovery (DR) environments.</p>
<ol dir="auto">
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Main/Branch:</strong></p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Name: <code>main</code> or <code>master</code></li>
<li>Purpose: This is the main branch that holds production-ready code. It's always stable and should ideally reflect the code running in the production environment.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Development Branch:</strong></p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Name: <code>develop</code> or <code>dev</code></li>
<li>Purpose: All ongoing development work takes place in this branch. New features and bug fixes are merged into this branch. It should be relatively stable but not necessarily production-ready at all times.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Feature Branches:</strong></p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Name: <code>feature/&lt;feature-name&gt;</code></li>
<li>Purpose: Each new feature or task gets its own branch, created from the <code>develop</code> branch. Developers work on these branches and merge them back into the <code>develop</code> branch when the feature is complete.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>QA Branch:</strong></p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Name: <code>qa</code> or <code>testing</code></li>
<li>Purpose: Once features are considered complete in the <code>develop</code> branch, they are merged into the <code>qa</code> branch for testing. This branch should reflect a stable state for testing purposes.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Pre-Production Branch:</strong></p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Name: <code>ppd</code> or <code>staging</code></li>
<li>Purpose: This branch is used to simulate the production environment closely. After successful QA testing, code is merged from the <code>qa</code> branch to the <code>ppd</code> branch for final validation before deployment.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Production Branch:</strong></p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Name: <code>prod</code> or <code>release</code></li>
<li>Purpose: Once the code is thoroughly tested in the <code>ppd</code> environment and ready for deployment, it's merged into the <code>prod</code> branch and deployed to the production environment.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Disaster Recovery Branch:</strong></p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Name: <code>dr</code> or <code>backup</code></li>
<li>Purpose: This branch holds code that is identical to the currently deployed production code. It's useful for disaster recovery scenarios, allowing rapid deployment of the latest stable code in case of critical issues.</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ol>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h1 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">50 Git commands</h1><a id="user-content-50-git-commands" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: 50 Git commands" href="#50-git-commands"><svg data-component="Octicon" class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>1. <code>git init</code></strong>
Initializes a new Git repository.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git init
Initialized empty Git repository in /path/to/repository/"><pre>$ git init
Initialized empty Git repository <span class="pl-k">in</span> /path/to/repository/</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>2. <code>git clone</code></strong>
Clones a remote repository to your local machine.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git clone https://github.com/username/repository.git
Cloning into 'repository'..."><pre>$ git clone https://github.com/username/repository.git
Cloning into <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>repository<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>...</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>3. <code>git add</code></strong>
Stages changes for commit.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git add file.txt"><pre>$ git add file.txt</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>4. <code>git status</code></strong>
Shows the status of the working directory and staged changes.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git status"><pre>$ git status</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>5. <code>git commit</code></strong>
Commits staged changes.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git commit -m &quot;Added new feature&quot;"><pre>$ git commit -m <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>Added new feature<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>6. <code>git log</code></strong>
Displays commit history.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git log"><pre>$ git log</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>7. <code>git diff</code></strong>
Shows differences between working directory and staged changes.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git diff"><pre>$ git diff</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>8. <code>git branch</code></strong>
Lists branches.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git branch"><pre>$ git branch</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>9. <code>git checkout</code></strong>
Switches branches or restores files.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git checkout branch_name"><pre>$ git checkout branch_name</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>10. <code>git merge</code></strong>
Merges changes from one branch into another.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git merge feature_branch"><pre>$ git merge feature_branch</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>11. <code>git pull</code></strong>
Fetches and integrates changes from a remote repository.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git pull origin master"><pre>$ git pull origin master</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>12. <code>git push</code></strong>
Pushes changes to a remote repository.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git push origin master"><pre>$ git push origin master</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>13. <code>git remote</code></strong>
Manages remote repositories.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git remote add origin https://github.com/username/repository.git"><pre>$ git remote add origin https://github.com/username/repository.git</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>14. <code>git fetch</code></strong>
Downloads objects and refs from a remote repository.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git fetch origin"><pre>$ git fetch origin</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>15. <code>git stash</code></strong>
Temporarily stores changes to work on something else.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git stash"><pre>$ git stash</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>16. <code>git tag</code></strong>
Creates and manages tags for specific commits.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git tag v1.0.0"><pre>$ git tag v1.0.0</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>17. <code>git reset</code></strong>
Unstages changes or moves the HEAD to a specific commit.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git reset HEAD file.txt"><pre>$ git reset HEAD file.txt</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>18. <code>git rebase</code></strong>
Reapplies commits on top of another base.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git rebase master"><pre>$ git rebase master</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>19. <code>git config</code></strong>
Sets configuration options.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git config --global user.name &quot;Your Name&quot;
$ git config --global user.email &quot;your.email@example.com&quot;"><pre>$ git config --global user.name <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>Your Name<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>
$ git config --global user.email <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>your.email@example.com<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>20. <code>git log --oneline</code></strong>
Displays compact commit history.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git log --oneline"><pre>$ git log --oneline</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>21. <code>git show</code></strong>
Shows information about a commit.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git show commit_hash"><pre>$ git show commit_hash</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>22. <code>git cherry-pick</code></strong>
Applies a commit from one branch to another.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git cherry-pick commit_hash"><pre>$ git cherry-pick commit_hash</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>23. <code>git rm</code></strong>
Removes files from the working directory and stages the removal.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git rm file.txt"><pre>$ git rm file.txt</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>24. <code>git revert</code></strong>
Creates a new commit that undoes changes from a previous commit.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git revert commit_hash"><pre>$ git revert commit_hash</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>25. <code>git reflog</code></strong>
Displays the history of HEAD positions.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git reflog"><pre>$ git reflog</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>26. <code>git clean</code></strong>
Removes untracked files and directories from the working directory.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git clean -n  # Dry-run
$ git clean -f  # Force removal"><pre>$ git clean -n  <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Dry-run</span>
$ git clean -f  <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Force removal</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>27. <code>git tag -a</code></strong>
Creates an annotated tag with a message.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git tag -a v1.0.0 -m &quot;Version 1.0.0&quot;"><pre>$ git tag -a v1.0.0 -m <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>Version 1.0.0<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>28. <code>git log --graph</code></strong>
Displays commit history as a graph.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git log --graph --oneline"><pre>$ git log --graph --oneline</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>29. <code>git config --list</code></strong>
Lists all Git configuration settings.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git config --list"><pre>$ git config --list</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>30. <code>git log --since</code> / <code>git log --until</code></strong>
Displays commit history within a time range.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git log --since=&quot;2 weeks ago&quot;
$ git log --until=&quot;2023-07-01&quot;"><pre>$ git log --since=<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>2 weeks ago<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>
$ git log --until=<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>2023-07-01<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>31. <code>git cherry</code></strong>
Shows commits that have not been merged.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git cherry master feature_branch"><pre>$ git cherry master feature_branch</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>32. <code>git revert --no-commit</code></strong>
Reverts changes interactively without committing.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git revert --no-commit commit_range"><pre>$ git revert --no-commit commit_range</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>33. <code>git log --author</code></strong>
Filters commit history by author.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git log --author=&quot;John Doe&quot;"><pre>$ git log --author=<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>John Doe<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>34. <code>git log --stat</code></strong>
Displays file statistics with commit history.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git log --stat"><pre>$ git log --stat</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>35. <code>git blame</code></strong>
Shows who last modified each line in a file.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git blame file.txt"><pre>$ git blame file.txt</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>36. <code>git tag -d</code></strong>
Deletes a tag.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git tag -d v1.0.0"><pre>$ git tag -d v1.0.0</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>37. <code>git log -p</code></strong>
Displays commit history with patch diffs.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git log -p"><pre>$ git log -p</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>38. <code>git rev-parse</code></strong>
Converts a revision string into a SHA-1 hash.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git rev-parse HEAD"><pre>$ git rev-parse HEAD</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>39. <code>git remote -v</code></strong>
Lists remote repositories and their URLs.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git remote -v"><pre>$ git remote -v</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>40. <code>git log --decorate</code></strong>
Displays references (branches, tags) in commit history.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git log --decorate"><pre>$ git log --decorate</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>41. <code>git bisect</code></strong>
Performs a binary search to find a faulty commit.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git bisect start
$ git bisect good &lt;commit&gt;
$ git bisect bad &lt;commit&gt;
$ git bisect reset"><pre>$ git bisect start
$ git bisect good <span class="pl-k">&lt;</span>commit<span class="pl-k">&gt;</span>
$ git bisect bad <span class="pl-k">&lt;</span>commit<span class="pl-k">&gt;</span>
$ git bisect reset</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>42. <code>git log --grep</code></strong>
Searches commit messages for a specific keyword.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git log --grep=&quot;bug fix&quot;"><pre>$ git log --grep=<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>bug fix<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>43. <code>git log --name-only</code></strong>
Displays only file names in commit history.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git log --name-only"><pre>$ git log --name-only</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>44. <code>git rebase -i</code></strong>
Interactively rewrites commit history.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git rebase -i HEAD~3"><pre>$ git rebase -i HEAD~3</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>45. <code>git log --before</code> / <code>git log --after</code></strong>
Displays commit history before/after a specific date.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git log --before=&quot;2023-01-01&quot;
$ git log --after=&quot;2022-01-01&quot;"><pre>$ git log --before=<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>2023-01-01<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>
$ git log --after=<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>2022-01-01<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>46. <code>git checkout -b</code></strong>
Creates a new branch and switches to it.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git checkout -b new_feature"><pre>$ git checkout -b new_feature</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>47. <code>git log --cherry-pick</code></strong>
Shows commits that have been cherry-picked.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git log --cherry-pick master..feature_branch"><pre>$ git log --cherry-pick master..feature_branch</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>48. <code>git log -S</code></strong>
Searches for changes that added or removed a specific string.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git log -S &quot;function_name&quot;"><pre>$ git log -S <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>function_name<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>49. <code>git reflog expire</code></strong>
Expires old reflog entries.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git reflog expire --expire=30.days refs/heads/master"><pre>$ git reflog expire --expire=30.days refs/heads/master</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>50. <code>git commit --amend</code></strong>
Modifies the most recent commit.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="$ git commit --amend"><pre>$ git commit --amend</pre></div>
